|- ( ph -> G e. ( ( A [,] B ) -cn-> RR ) )

Essential: cmvth.df


|- ( ph -> dom ( RR _D F ) = ( A (,) B ) )

Essential: cmvth.dg


|- ( ph -> dom ( RR _D G ) = ( A (,) B ) )

Cauchy's Mean Value Theorem. If F , G are real continuous functions on [ A , B ] differentiable on ( A , B ) , then there is some x e. ( A , B ) such that F ' ( x ) / G ' ( x ) = ( F ( A ) - F ( B ) ) / ( G ( A ) - G ( B ) ) . (We express the condition without division, so that we need no nonzero constraints.) (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 29-Dec-2016.)

Theorem: cmvth


|- ( ph -> E. x e. ( A (,) B ) ( ( ( F ` B ) - ( F ` A ) ) x. ( ( RR _D G ) ` x ) ) = ( ( ( G ` B ) - ( G ` A ) ) x. ( ( RR _D F ) ` x ) ) )

Essential: mvth.d


|- ( ph -> dom ( RR _D F ) = ( A (,) B ) )

The Mean Value Theorem. If F is a real continuous function on [ A , B ] which is differentiable on ( A , B ) , then there is some x e. ( A , B ) such that ( RR _D F ) `` x is equal to the average slope over [ A , B ] . This is Metamath 100 proof #75. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 1-Sep-2014.) (Proof shortened by Mario Carneiro, 29-Dec-2016.)

Theorem: mvth


|- ( ph -> E. x e. ( A (,) B ) ( ( RR _D F ) ` x ) = ( ( ( F ` B ) - ( F ` A ) ) / ( B - A ) ) )

A function with derivative bounded by M is Lipschitz continuous with Lipschitz constant equal to M . (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 3-Mar-2015.)

Essential: dvlipcn.x


|- ( ph -> X C_ CC )

Essential: dvlipcn.f


|- ( ph -> F : X --> CC )

Essential: dvlipcn.a


|- ( ph -> A e. CC )

Essential: dvlipcn.r


|- ( ph -> R e. RR* )

Essential: dvlipcn.b


|- B = ( A ( ball ` ( abs o. - ) ) R )

Essential: dvlipcn.d


|- ( ph -> B C_ dom ( CC _D F ) )

Essential: dvlipcn.m


|- ( ph -> M e. RR )

Essential: dvlipcn.l


|- ( ( ph /\ x e. B ) -> ( abs ` ( ( CC _D F ) ` x ) ) <_ M )

A complex function with derivative bounded by M on an open ball is Lipschitz continuous with Lipschitz constant equal to M . (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 18-Mar-2015.)

If a continuous function has zero derivative at all points on the interior of a closed interval, then it must be a constant function. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 2-Sep-2014.) (Proof shortened by Mario Carneiro, 3-Mar-2015.)

L'Hôpital's Rule for limits from the right. If F and G are differentiable real functions on ( A , B ) , and F and G both approach 0 at A , and G ( x ) and G ' ( x ) are not zero on ( A , B ) , and the limit of F ' ( x ) / G ' ( x ) at A is C , then the limit F ( x ) / G ( x ) at A also exists and equals C . (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 29-Dec-2016.)

Theorem: lhop1


|- ( ph -> C e. ( ( z e. ( A (,) B ) |-> ( ( F ` z ) / ( G ` z ) ) ) limCC A ) )

Essential: lhop2.a


|- ( ph -> A e. RR* )

Essential: lhop2.b


|- ( ph -> B e. RR )

Essential: lhop2.l


|- ( ph -> A < B )

Essential: lhop2.f


|- ( ph -> F : ( A (,) B ) --> RR )

Essential: lhop2.g


|- ( ph -> G : ( A (,) B ) --> RR )

Essential: lhop2.if


|- ( ph -> dom ( RR _D F ) = ( A (,) B ) )

Essential: lhop2.ig


|- ( ph -> dom ( RR _D G ) = ( A (,) B ) )

Essential: lhop2.f0


|- ( ph -> 0 e. ( F limCC B ) )

Essential: lhop2.g0


|- ( ph -> 0 e. ( G limCC B ) )

Essential: lhop2.gn0


|- ( ph -> -. 0 e. ran G )

Essential: lhop2.gd0


|- ( ph -> -. 0 e. ran ( RR _D G ) )

Essential: lhop2.c


|- ( ph -> C e. ( ( z e. ( A (,) B ) |-> ( ( ( RR _D F ) ` z ) / ( ( RR _D G ) ` z ) ) ) limCC B ) )

L'Hôpital's Rule for limits from the left. If F and G are differentiable real functions on ( A , B ) , and F and G both approach 0 at B , and G ( x ) and G ' ( x ) are not zero on ( A , B ) , and the limit of F ' ( x ) / G ' ( x ) at B is C , then the limit F ( x ) / G ( x ) at B also exists and equals C . (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 29-Dec-2016.)

Theorem: lhop2


|- ( ph -> C e. ( ( z e. ( A (,) B ) |-> ( ( F ` z ) / ( G ` z ) ) ) limCC B ) )

Essential: lhop.a


|- ( ph -> A C_ RR )

Essential: lhop.f


|- ( ph -> F : A --> RR )

Essential: lhop.g


|- ( ph -> G : A --> RR )

Essential: lhop.i


|- ( ph -> I e. ( topGen ` ran (,) ) )

Essential: lhop.b


|- ( ph -> B e. I )

Essential: lhop.d


|- D = ( I \ { B } )

Essential: lhop.if


|- ( ph -> D C_ dom ( RR _D F ) )

Essential: lhop.ig


|- ( ph -> D C_ dom ( RR _D G ) )

Essential: lhop.f0


|- ( ph -> 0 e. ( F limCC B ) )

Essential: lhop.g0


|- ( ph -> 0 e. ( G limCC B ) )

Essential: lhop.gn0


|- ( ph -> -. 0 e. ( G " D ) )

Essential: lhop.gd0


|- ( ph -> -. 0 e. ( ( RR _D G ) " D ) )

Essential: lhop.c


|- ( ph -> C e. ( ( z e. D |-> ( ( ( RR _D F ) ` z ) / ( ( RR _D G ) ` z ) ) ) limCC B ) )

L'Hôpital's Rule. If I is an open set of the reals, F and G are real functions on A containing all of I except possibly B , which are differentiable everywhere on I \ { B } , F and G both approach 0, and the limit of F ' ( x ) / G ' ( x ) at B is C , then the limit F ( x ) / G ( x ) at B also exists and equals C . This is Metamath 100 proof #64. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 30-Dec-2016.)

Theorem: lhop


|- ( ph -> C e. ( ( z e. D |-> ( ( F ` z ) / ( G ` z ) ) ) limCC B ) )

The derivative rule for inverse functions. If F is a continuous and differentiable bijective function from X to Y which never has derivative 0 , then ``' F is also differentiable, and its derivative is the reciprocal of the derivative of F . (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 24-Feb-2015.)

A real function with strictly increasing derivative is strictly convex. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 20-Jun-2015.)

Theorem: dvcvx


|- ( ph -> ( F ` C ) < ( ( T x. ( F ` A ) ) + ( ( 1 - T ) x. ( F ` B ) ) ) )

The reverse of ~ dvfsumrlim , when comparing a finite sum of increasing terms to an integral. In this case there is no point in stating the limit properties, because the terms of the sum aren't approaching zero, but there is nevertheless still a natural asymptotic statement that can be made. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 20-May-2016.)

|- ( ph -> E e. RR+ )

Essential: ftc1.r


|- ( ph -> R e. RR+ )

Essential: ftc1.fc

Essential: ftc1.x2

The Fundamental Theorem of Calculus, part one. The function formed by varying the right endpoint of an integral is differentiable at C with derivative F ( C ) if the original function is continuous at C . This is part of Metamath 100 proof #15. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 1-Sep-2014.)

Strengthen the assumptions of ~ ftc1 to when the function F is continuous on the entire interval ( A , B ) ; in this case we can calculate _D G exactly. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 1-Sep-2014.)

The Fundamental Theorem of Calculus, part two. If F is a function continuous on [ A , B ] and continuously differentiable on ( A , B ) , then the integral of the derivative of F is equal to F ( B ) - F ( A ) . This is part of Metamath 100 proof #15. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 2-Sep-2014.)

Essential: itgparts.c

Essential: itgparts.e


|- ( ( ph /\ x = X ) -> ( A x. C ) = E )

Essential: itgparts.f


|- ( ( ph /\ x = Y ) -> ( A x. C ) = F )

Integration by parts. If B ( x ) is the derivative of A ( x ) and D ( x ) is the derivative of C ( x ) , and E = ( A x. B ) ( X ) and F = ( A x. B ) ( Y ) , then under suitable integrability and differentiability assumptions, the integral of A x. D from X to Y is equal to F - E minus the integral of B x. C . (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 3-Sep-2014.)

Theorem: itgparts


|- ( ph -> S. ( X (,) Y ) ( A x. D ) _d x = ( ( F - E ) - S. ( X (,) Y ) ( B x. C ) _d x ) )

Integration by u -substitution. If A ( x ) is a continuous, differentiable function from [ X , Y ] to ( Z , W ) , whose derivative is continuous and integrable, and C ( u ) is a continuous function on ( Z , W ) , then the integral of C ( u ) from K = A ( X ) to L = A ( Y ) is equal to the integral of C ( A ( x ) ) _D A ( x ) from X to Y . In this part of the proof we discharge the assumptions in ~ itgsubstlem , which use the fact that ( Z , W ) is open to shrink the interval a little to ( M , N ) where Z < M < N < W - this is possible because A ( x ) is a continuous function on a closed interval, so its range is in fact a closed interval, and we have some wiggle room on the edges. (Contributed by Mario Carneiro, 7-Sep-2014.)

Theorem: itgsubst


|- ( ph -> S_ [ K -> L ] C _d u = S_ [ X -> Y ] ( E x. B ) _d x )
